## Tool Selection

| Goal | Tool |

**Decision logic:**
1. Know the exact symbol? → `sg_keyword_search`
2. Know the concept, not the name? → `sg_nls_search`
3. Need definition of a symbol? → `sg_go_to_definition`
4. Need all callers/references? → `sg_find_references`
5. Need full file content? → `sg_read_file`

## Scoping (Always Do This)

```
repo:^github.com/ORG/REPO$           # Exact repo (preferred)
repo:github.com/ORG/                 # All repos in org
file:.*\.ts$                         # TypeScript only
file:src/api/                        # Specific directory
```

Start narrow. Expand only if results are empty.

## Efficiency Rules

- Chain searches logically: search → read → references → definition
- Don't re-search for the same pattern; use results from prior calls
- Prefer `sg_keyword_search` over `sg_nls_search` when you have exact terms
- Read 2-3 related files before synthesising, rather than one at a time
- Don't read 20+ remote files without writing code — once you understand the pattern, start implementing

## If Stuck

If MCP search returns no results:
1. Broaden the search query (synonyms, partial identifiers)
2. Try `sg_nls_search` for semantic matching
3. Use `sg_list_files` to browse the directory structure
4. Use `sg_list_repos` to verify the repository name

# Platform Engineering: CODEOWNERS Infrastructure Discovery

## Your Task

Your platform team needs to understand how code ownership works in Grafana — not just the CODEOWNERS file itself, but the entire infrastructure around it: manifest generation, CI validation, Go integration with feature management, and npm scripts.

**Specific question**: Find all files in `grafana/grafana` that form the CODEOWNERS infrastructure:

1. **The actual CODEOWNERS file** — the GitHub ownership definition
2. **CI workflows** that validate CODEOWNERS
3. **Manifest generation scripts** (JavaScript) that parse and index CODEOWNERS
4. **Go code** that defines the `codeowner` type for feature management
5. **npm scripts** that orchestrate manifest generation

This crosses YAML (CI), JavaScript (scripts), Go (backend), and file ownership conventions.

## Context

You are a platform engineer investigating how code ownership is implemented and enforced in a large monorepo. Understanding this infrastructure is critical for onboarding new teams, debugging CI failures related to CODEOWNERS validation, and extending the ownership system to new areas of the codebase.

## Available Resources

Your ecosystem includes the following repositories:
- `grafana/grafana` at v11.4.0

## Output Format

Create a file at `/workspace/answer.json` with your findings in the following structure:

```json
{
  "files": [
    {"repo": "grafana/grafana", "path": "relative/path/to/file"}
  ],
  "text": "Narrative explanation of the CODEOWNERS infrastructure."
}
```

**Important**: Use `"grafana/grafana"` for the repo name. Strip `github.com/` prefix.
**Note**: Sourcegraph MCP tools return repo names with a `github.com/` prefix (e.g., `github.com/grafana/grafana`). Strip this prefix in your answer.

Include only the `files` field. Your answer is evaluated against a closed-world oracle — completeness matters.

## Evaluation

Your answer will be scored on:
- **File recall and precision**: Did you find all files that form the CODEOWNERS infrastructure?
- **Keyword presence**: Does your answer reference key identifiers (CODEOWNERS, codeowners-manifest, codeowner)?

The system spans CI/CD validation, Go feature toggle management, and npm scripts for manifest generation.\\n\\nAt the core is .github/CODEOWNERS, the GitHub ownership file that defines which teams own which code paths. This file is validated in CI by the .github/workflows/codeowners-validator.yml workflow, which runs the mszostok/codeowners-validator GitHub Action to ensure the CODEOWNERS file is syntactically correct and covers all necessary paths.\\n\\nThe Go feature management infrastructure uses a custom codeowner type defined in pkg/services/featuremgmt/codeowners.go. This type represents GitHub teams and users (e.g., @grafana/grafana-app-platform-squad). Feature flags are defined in pkg/services/featuremgmt/registry.go, where each feature toggle has an Owner field of type codeowner. The FeatureFlag struct in pkg/services/featuremgmt/models.go includes the Owner field (of type codeowner), and the corresponding Kubernetes API type definition in pkg/apis/featuretoggle/v0alpha1/types.go defines the codeowner field in the FeatureSpec.\\n\\nManifest generation is orchestrated through pkg/services/featuremgmt/toggles_gen_test.go, which generates three critical files:\\n- toggles_gen.json: A Kubernetes FeatureList resource containing metadata about all features including their codeowners\\n- toggles_gen.go: Generated Go code for feature flag registration\\n- toggles_gen.csv: A CSV export of feature toggles with their properties\\n\\nThe generation is triggered via the Makefile target gen-feature-toggles, which runs Go tests that regenerate these manifest files based on the registry.go definitions.\\n\\nOn the frontend side, scripts/cli/generateBettererIssues.ts is a TypeScript script that uses the npm codeowners package to parse the CODEOWNERS file and route code quality issues to the appropriate team owners. This script is invoked via the yarn betterer:issues npm script defined in package.json, enabling automated issue assignment based on file ownership.\\n\\nThe contribute/feature-toggles.md documentation guides developers through the feature toggle workflow, directing them to update registry.go and then run the test generation. The complete infrastructure ensures that code ownership is tracked through every layer: from GitHub's CODEOWNERS for PR reviews, through Go's feature management system with codeowner types, to generated manifests that can be queried and displayed in the UI, to npm scripts that route quality issues to the correct team owners.\"\n}\n",

The system spans CI/CD validation, Go feature toggle management, and npm scripts for manifest generation.\\n\\nAt the core is .github/CODEOWNERS, the GitHub ownership file that defines which teams own which code paths. This file is validated in CI by the .github/workflows/codeowners-validator.yml workflow, which runs the mszostok/codeowners-validator GitHub Action to ensure the CODEOWNERS file is syntactically correct and covers all necessary paths.\\n\\nThe Go feature management infrastructure uses a custom codeowner type defined in pkg/services/featuremgmt/codeowners.go. This script is invoked via the yarn betterer:issues npm script defined in package.json, enabling automated issue assignment based on file ownership.\\n\\nThe contribute/feature-toggles.md documentation guides developers through the feature toggle workflow, directing them to update registry.go and then run the test generation. The complete infrastructure ensures that code ownership is tracked through every layer: from GitHub's CODEOWNERS for PR reviews, through Go's feature management system with codeowner types, to generated manifests that can be queried and displayed in the UI, to npm scripts that route quality issues to the correct team owners.\"\n}\n",
